   <div class="marriage-line-margin2px">&#8203;</div>&#32;<div style="display:inline-block;margin-bottom:1px;">&#8203;</div>&#40;<abbr title="married">m.</abbr>&#160;1996&#59;&#32;<abbr title="divorced">div.</abbr>&#160;2000&#41;<wbr />&#8203;</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">10</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><b>Musical career</b></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Origin</th><td class="infobox-data">Los Angeles, California</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Genres</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">

<li><a href="/wiki/G-funk" title="G-funk">G-funk</a><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Boy_Records" title="Tommy Boy Records">Tommy Boy</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warner_Records" title="Warner Records">Warner Bros. Records</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Allied_Artists_Music_Group" title="Allied Artists Music Group">Allied Artists Music Group</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/WC_and_the_Maad_Circle" title="WC and the Maad Circle">WC and the Maad Circle</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Artis Leon Ivey Jr.</b> (August 1, 1963 – September 28, 2022),<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> known by his stage name <b>Coolio</b>, was an American rapper. He was best known for his singles "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta%27s_Paradise" title="Gangsta&#39;s Paradise">Gangsta's Paradise</a>" (1995), which won a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>, and was credited for changing the course of hip hop by bringing it to a wider audience,<sup id="cite_ref-course_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-course-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Voyage_(Coolio_song)" title="Fantastic Voyage (Coolio song)">Fantastic Voyage</a>" (1994), "<a href="/wiki/1,_2,_3,_4_(Sumpin%27_New)" title="1, 2, 3, 4 (Sumpin&#39; New)">1, 2, 3, 4 (Sumpin' New)</a>" (1996), and "<a href="/wiki/C_U_When_U_Get_There" title="C U When U Get There">C U When U Get There</a>" (1997). He released nine albums, the first three of which achieved mainstream success: <i><a href="/wiki/It_Takes_a_Thief_(album)" title="It Takes a Thief (album)">It Takes a Thief</a></i> (1994), <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta%27s_Paradise_(album)" title="Gangsta&#39;s Paradise (album)">Gangsta's Paradise</a></i> (1995), and <i><a href="/wiki/My_Soul_(Coolio_album)" title="My Soul (Coolio album)">My Soul</a></i> (1997). Coolio first achieved recognition as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a> group <a href="/wiki/WC_and_the_Maad_Circle" title="WC and the Maad Circle">WC and the Maad Circle</a>. His nickname, originally "Coolio Iglesias", was a takeoff of <a href="/wiki/Julio_Iglesias" title="Julio Iglesias">Julio Iglesias</a>. Coolio sold 4.8 million albums in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He also created the 6-episode reality television show <i><a href="/wiki/Coolio%27s_Rules" title="Coolio&#39;s Rules">Coolio's Rules</a></i> (2008), the web series <i><a href="/wiki/Cookin%27_with_Coolio" title="Cookin&#39; with Coolio">Cookin' with Coolio</a></i> and released a cookbook.
</p><p>Coolio died on September 2022, aged 59, from an accidental overdose of <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine" title="Methamphetamine">methamphetamine</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Artis Leon Ivey Jr. was born on August 1, 1963, in <a href="/wiki/Monessen,_Pennsylvania" title="Monessen, Pennsylvania">Monessen, Pennsylvania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cbsobit_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbsobit-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-varietyobit_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-varietyobit-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nbcobit_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbcobit-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cbsobit_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbsobit-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> His mother was a factory worker who divorced his father, who was a carpenter, and they moved to <a href="/wiki/Compton,_California" title="Compton, California">Compton, California</a> when Ivey was eight years old.<sup id="cite_ref-kemp_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kemp-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Ivey was severely <a href="/wiki/Asthmatic" class="mw-redirect" title="Asthmatic">asthmatic</a> and, as a child, he was taken to the hospital several times due to asthma complications. He was a regular visitor to his local library as a boy. He often played board games with his mother.<sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He started rapping as a teenager, earning the nickname Coolio Iglesias due to his slick performances, a takeoff of Spanish singer <a href="/wiki/Julio_Iglesias" title="Julio Iglesias">Julio Iglesias</a>; the nickname was later shortened to Coolio.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He was arrested for taking a weapon to school and served prison time for <a href="/wiki/Larceny" title="Larceny">larceny</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-course_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-course-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> As Compton went into decline in the 1980s, he became addicted to <a href="/wiki/Crack_cocaine" title="Crack cocaine">crack cocaine</a>, but quit drugs after spending time living with his father in <a href="/wiki/San_Jose,_California" title="San Jose, California">San Jose</a>, crediting <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> for helping him get over his addiction.<sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> There, he worked for the <a href="/wiki/California_Department_of_Forestry_and_Fire_Protection" title="California Department of Forestry and Fire Protection">California Department of Forestry and Fire Protection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kemp_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kemp-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Coolio attended <a href="/wiki/Compton_Community_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Compton Community College">Compton Community College</a> then worked in a <a href="/wiki/Volunteer_fire_department" title="Volunteer fire department">volunteer fire department</a> and security at <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>, before becoming a rapper.<sup id="cite_ref-Allmusic_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Music career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Coolio recorded his first single in 1987, titled "Whatcha Gonna Do?".<sup id="cite_ref-Berry_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berry-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> In 1988, he recorded "What Makes You Dance (Force Groove)" with Nu-Skool. Coolio made connections in the L.A. rap scene, and in 1991, joined the group <a href="/wiki/WC_and_the_Maad_Circle" title="WC and the Maad Circle">WC and the Maad Circle</a>, led by rapper <a href="/wiki/WC_(rapper)" title="WC (rapper)">WC</a>. He is a credited co-contributor on the group's debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_a_Damn_Thang_Changed" title="Ain&#39;t a Damn Thang Changed">Ain't a Damn Thang Changed</a></i>, including on the single "Dress Code".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tommy_Boy_Records_and_It_Takes_a_Thief">Tommy Boy Records and <i>It Takes a Thief</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tommy Boy Records and It Takes a Thief">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1994, Coolio signed a <a href="/wiki/Recording_contract" title="Recording contract">recording contract</a> with <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Boy_Records" title="Tommy Boy Records">Tommy Boy Records</a> and released his debut solo album <i><a href="/wiki/It_Takes_a_Thief_(album)" title="It Takes a Thief (album)">It Takes a Thief</a></i>. The lead single "<a href="/wiki/Fantastic_Voyage_(Coolio_song)" title="Fantastic Voyage (Coolio song)">Fantastic Voyage</a>" received heavy rotation on <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> and peaked at No. 3 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, becoming one of the biggest rap singles of the year. Other minor hits from the album include "County Line" and "I Remember". <i>It Takes a Thief</i> peaked at No. 8 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> becoming certified Platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The album received praise for bringing a humorous and lighthearted perspective to the often violent and profane themes of typical <a href="/wiki/Gangsta_rap" title="Gangsta rap">gangsta rap</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Allmusic_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Gangsta.27s_Paradise"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Gangsta's_Paradise"><i>Gangsta's Paradise</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Gangsta&#039;s Paradise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1995, for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Dangerous_Minds" title="Dangerous Minds">Dangerous Minds</a></i>, Coolio released "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta%27s_Paradise" title="Gangsta&#39;s Paradise">Gangsta's Paradise</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> singer <a href="/wiki/L.V._(singer)" title="L.V. (singer)">L.V.</a>. It became one of the most successful rap songs of all time, topping the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for three weeks. It was the No. 1 single of 1995 in the United States for all genres and was a global hit topping the United Kingdom, Ireland, France, Germany, Italy, Sweden, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, Netherlands, Norway, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>, Australia, and New Zealand charts. "Gangsta's Paradise" was the second-best-selling single of 1995 in the U.K. The song also created a controversy when Coolio claimed that comedy musician <a href="/wiki/%22Weird_Al%22_Yankovic" title="&quot;Weird Al&quot; Yankovic">"Weird Al" Yankovic</a> had not asked for permission to make his parody of "Gangsta's Paradise", titled "<a href="/wiki/Amish_Paradise" title="Amish Paradise">Amish Paradise</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1996_Grammy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="1996 Grammy Awards">1996 Grammy Awards</a>, the song won Coolio a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance">Grammy Award for Best Rap Solo Performance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-grammy_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Originally "Gangsta's Paradise" was not meant to be included in one of Coolio's studio albums, but due to its success, Coolio included it on the album, making it the title track. It <a href="/wiki/Interpolation_(popular_music)" title="Interpolation (popular music)">interpolates</a> the chorus and music of the song "<a href="/wiki/Pastime_Paradise" title="Pastime Paradise">Pastime Paradise</a>" by Stevie Wonder, which was recorded nearly 20 years earlier on Wonder's album <i><a href="/wiki/Songs_in_the_Key_of_Life" title="Songs in the Key of Life">Songs in the Key of Life</a></i>. The album <i><a href="/wiki/Gangsta%27s_Paradise_(album)" title="Gangsta&#39;s Paradise (album)">Gangsta's Paradise</a></i> was released in 1995 and was certified two-times Platinum by the RIAA, selling more than two&#160;million copies in the US alone.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album contains two other major hits in "<a href="/wiki/1,_2,_3,_4_(Sumpin%27_New)" title="1, 2, 3, 4 (Sumpin&#39; New)">1, 2, 3, 4 (Sumpin' New)</a>" and "Too Hot" with J.&#160;T.&#160;Taylor of <a href="/wiki/Kool_%26_the_Gang" title="Kool &amp; the Gang">Kool &amp; the Gang</a> doing the chorus.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Despite no longer being an official member of the group, Coolio appears on the second WC and the Maad Circle album <i><a href="/wiki/Curb_Servin%27" title="Curb Servin&#39;">Curb Servin'</a></i> on the song "In a Twist".<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, Coolio had another top 40 hit with the song "It's All the Way Live (Now)" from the <a href="/wiki/Eddie_(soundtrack)" title="Eddie (soundtrack)">soundtrack</a> to the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Eddie_(film)" title="Eddie (film)">Eddie</a></i>. He is also featured on the song "Hit 'em High" from the soundtrack to the 1996 film <i><a href="/wiki/Space_Jam" title="Space Jam">Space Jam</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/B-Real" title="B-Real">B-Real</a>, <a href="/wiki/Method_Man" title="Method Man">Method Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the band <a href="/wiki/Falling_in_Reverse" title="Falling in Reverse">Falling in Reverse</a> did a cover of "Gangsta's Paradise" for <i><a href="/wiki/Punk_Goes_90s_Vol._2" title="Punk Goes 90s Vol. 2">Punk Goes 90s Vol. 2</a></i>, with Coolio making a cameo in the music video.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Red_Hot_Organization_and_Tommy_Boy_Records_dismissal">Red Hot Organization and Tommy Boy Records dismissal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Red Hot Organization and Tommy Boy Records dismissal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1996, Coolio appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Red_Hot_Organization" title="Red Hot Organization">Red Hot Organization</a>'s compilation CD <i><a href="/wiki/America_Is_Dying_Slowly" title="America Is Dying Slowly">America Is Dying Slowly</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Biz_Markie" title="Biz Markie">Biz Markie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wu-Tang_Clan" title="Wu-Tang Clan">Wu-Tang Clan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a>, among many other prominent hip-hop artists. The CD meant to raise awareness of the AIDS epidemic among African-American men.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> That same year, he recorded the music video "Aw, Here It Goes!" for the opening sequence of the <a href="/wiki/Nickelodeon" title="Nickelodeon">Nickelodeon</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Kenan_%26_Kel" title="Kenan &amp; Kel">Kenan &amp; Kel</a></i>, which ran for four seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-kenankel_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kenankel-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_(cropped).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-Coolio_at_The_Great_GoogaMooga_Festival_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2466" data-file-height="2632" /></a><figcaption>Coolio in 2012</figcaption></figure>
<p>Coolio's third solo album, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Soul_(Coolio_album)" title="My Soul (Coolio album)">My Soul</a></i>, came out in 1997. Although it contains the major hit "<a href="/wiki/C_U_When_U_Get_There" title="C U When U Get There">C U When U Get There</a>" and the album went gold, it failed to reach the success of his previous two albums. Coolio was subsequently dropped from the <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Boy_Records" title="Tommy Boy Records">Tommy Boy Records</a> label. Since then, 2001's <i><a href="/wiki/Coolio.com" title="Coolio.com">Coolio.com</a></i>, 2003's <i><a href="/wiki/El_Cool_Magnifico" title="El Cool Magnifico">El Cool Magnifico</a></i>, 2006's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_Gangsta" title="The Return of the Gangsta">The Return of the Gangsta</a></i>, and 2008's <i><a href="/wiki/Steal_Hear" title="Steal Hear">Steal Hear</a></i>, 2009's <a href="/wiki/From_the_Bottom_2_the_Top" title="From the Bottom 2 the Top">From the Bottom 2 the Top</a>, and 2017's <i>Long Live the Thief</i> have not charted on any <a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts"><i>Billboard</i> chart</a>. He did have a minor hit in the UK in 2006 with "<a href="/wiki/Gangsta_Walk" title="Gangsta Walk">Gangsta Walk</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Snoop_Dogg" title="Snoop Dogg">Snoop Dogg</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While touring with hip-hop duo <a href="/wiki/Insane_Clown_Posse" title="Insane Clown Posse">Insane Clown Posse</a>, Coolio received a tattoo as a homage to the group's fanbase, reading "<a href="/wiki/Juggalo" title="Juggalo">Jugalo</a> Cool" &#32;&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>&#93;. He stated that the misspelling was intentional. Coolio performed at the <a href="/wiki/Gathering_of_the_Juggalos" title="Gathering of the Juggalos">Gathering of the Juggalos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coolio is featured on an international collaboration track called "Fuck the DJ" by UK rapper Blacklisted MC, also featuring <a href="/wiki/Bizarre_(rapper)" title="Bizarre (rapper)">Bizarre</a> of <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>, <a href="/wiki/Adil_Omar" title="Adil Omar">Adil Omar</a> (from Pakistan), and <a href="/wiki/Uzimon" title="Uzimon">Uzimon</a> (from Bermuda). The song premiered on music website Noisey from <a href="/wiki/Vice_(magazine)" title="Vice (magazine)"><i>Vice</i></a> in October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television_appearances">Television appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Television appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Coolio appeared as a contestant on <i>Comeback – Die große Chance</i> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> (translated in English as <i>Comeback: The Big Chance</i>), a German talent show featuring artists looking for a comeback.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the television series <a href="/wiki/Futurama" title="Futurama">Futurama</a>, Coolio made three appearances on the TV series and one appearance in <a href="/wiki/Futurama:_Bender%27s_Big_Score" title="Futurama: Bender&#39;s Big Score">Futurama: Bender's Big Score</a>, a straight-to-video movie for the show. He played Kwanzaa-bot, a rapping robot who spreads awareness about <a href="/wiki/Kwanzaa" title="Kwanzaa">Kwanzaa</a>. His final appearance in the episode "<i>I Know What You Did Next Xmas</i>" was dedicated to him, as he had recorded his lines for the episode just weeks prior to his death.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Coolio appeared as a housemate on <i><a href="/wiki/Celebrity_Big_Brother_6" class="mw-redirect" title="Celebrity Big Brother 6">Celebrity Big Brother 6</a></i>, which he placed 3rd. He later went to appear on the UK's <i><a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Big_Brother" title="Ultimate Big Brother">Ultimate Big Brother</a></i> in 2010, where he decided it was best to leave the house after numerous confrontations with <a href="/wiki/Nadia_Almada" title="Nadia Almada">Nadia Almada</a> and others there. In January 2012, he was one of eight celebrities participating in the <a href="/wiki/Food_Network" title="Food Network">Food Network</a> reality television series <i><a href="/wiki/Rachael_vs._Guy:_Celebrity_Cook-Off" title="Rachael vs. Guy: Celebrity Cook-Off">Rachael vs. Guy: Celebrity Cook-Off</a></i>, where he represented the <a href="/wiki/Music_Saves_Lives" title="Music Saves Lives">Music Saves Lives</a> Organization.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He also made a <a href="/wiki/Guest_appearance" title="Guest appearance">guest appearance</a> as himself on <i><a href="/wiki/Sabrina_the_Teenage_Witch" title="Sabrina the Teenage Witch">Sabrina the Teenage Witch</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-sabrina_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sabrina-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coolio is featured on the March 5, 2013, episode of the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a> reality program <i><a href="/wiki/Wife_Swap_(American_TV_series)" title="Wife Swap (American TV series)">Wife Swap</a></i>, but his then-girlfriend left him after the program was taped.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> On June 30, 2013, he appeared alongside comedian <a href="/wiki/Jenny_Eclair" title="Jenny Eclair">Jenny Eclair</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Emmerdale" title="Emmerdale">Emmerdale</a></i> actor <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Wolfenden_(actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthew Wolfenden (actor)">Matthew Wolfenden</a> on the UK game show <i><a href="/wiki/Tipping_Point_(game_show)" title="Tipping Point (game show)">Tipping Point: Lucky Stars</a></i>, where he came in second. On June 30, 2012, Coolio voiced a wax figure of himself on <i><a href="/wiki/Gravity_Falls" title="Gravity Falls">Gravity Falls</a></i>. He also appears on "Homie-Work", a 1998 episode of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Nanny" title="The Nanny">The Nanny</a></i>, in which he portrays a nerdy man, a "gift wrapper", transformed by the Jewish nanny into a "Rapper" for <a href="/wiki/Maxwell_Sheffield" class="mw-redirect" title="Maxwell Sheffield">Maxwell Sheffield</a>'s new rap musical.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coolio guest starred on a 2014 episode of the <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Jesus_(TV_series)" title="Black Jesus (TV series)">Black Jesus</a></i> titled "Gangsta's Paradise".<sup id="cite_ref-blackjesus_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blackjesus-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In July 2016, Coolio performed on ABC's <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(TV_series)" title="Greatest Hits (TV series)">Greatest Hits</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_appearances">Other appearances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other appearances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2019, Coolio appeared on the Irish rap group Versatile's track "Escape Wagon". He later featured on their 2021 album, <i>Fuck Versatile</i>, on the track "Coolio Interlude".<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Coolio had ten children,<sup id="cite_ref-clark_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clark-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> one of whom was born to his wife, Josefa Salinas, whom he married in 1996 and divorced in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-cooliosrules_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cooliosrules-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In March 2022, he told Australia's <i><a href="/wiki/Today_Extra" title="Today Extra">Today Extra</a></i> that he had five grandchildren.<sup id="cite_ref-clark_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-clark-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2008, Coolio and jazz saxophonist Jarez were enlisted as spokespersons by the group Environmental Justice and Climate Change to educate students at <a href="/wiki/Historically_black_colleges_and_universities" title="Historically black colleges and universities">historically black colleges and universities</a> about <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Coolio was a spokesperson for the <a href="/wiki/Asthma_and_Allergy_Foundation_of_America" title="Asthma and Allergy Foundation of America">Asthma and Allergy Foundation of America</a> and he and his children are <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a> sufferers.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He had a web-based cooking show called <i><a href="/wiki/Cookin%27_with_Coolio" title="Cookin&#39; with Coolio">Cookin' with Coolio</a></i>, an offshoot of his reality show, <i><a href="/wiki/Coolio%27s_Rules" title="Coolio&#39;s Rules">Coolio's Rules</a></i> that ran for six episodes in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-outta_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outta-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Coolio was the running mate for <a href="/wiki/Pornographic_film_actor" title="Pornographic film actor">pornographic film actress</a> Cherie DeVille's <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> presidential run in the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election" title="2020 United States presidential election">2020 United States presidential election</a>; they ended their campaign in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, a court in <a href="/wiki/B%C3%B6blingen" title="Böblingen">Böblingen</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a>, sentenced Coolio to six months probation and fined him $17,000 after convicting him of being an accessory to robbery and causing bodily injury after Coolio and his band members allegedly attempted <a href="/wiki/Shoplifting" title="Shoplifting">shoplifting</a> clothing worth $940 and then punched the store owner when he was caught. Coolio alleged that he was promised the clothing for free in exchange for signing autographs.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Coolio and members of his crew were arrested for having a loaded firearm inside of a bag at <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_International_Airport" title="Los Angeles International Airport">Los Angeles International Airport</a>. The bag was flagged by the <a href="/wiki/Transportation_Security_Administration" title="Transportation Security Administration">Transportation Security Administration</a> as the group attempted to pass through a security checkpoint. One of his bodyguards claimed ownership of the bag, but Coolio later admitted that he was the owner. Coolio was sentenced to three years of probation and 45 days of <a href="/wiki/Community_service" title="Community service">community service</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, Coolio missed a performance after he was denied entry into Singapore upon landing at <a href="/wiki/Changi_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Changi International Airport">Changi International Airport</a>. Singapore's <a href="/wiki/Immigration_and_Checkpoints_Authority" title="Immigration and Checkpoints Authority">Immigration and Checkpoints Authority</a> declined to comment on the reason for the denial, citing reasons of confidentiality. Coolio had been traveling from Beijing to Singapore to perform at a Formula One concert event.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death">Death</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Death">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On September 28, 2022, while at a friend's house in Los Angeles, California, Coolio, at the age of 59, was discovered unresponsive on the bathroom floor and was pronounced dead by first responders.<sup id="cite_ref-nbcobit_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nbcobit-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Department_of_Medical_Examiner-Coroner" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Angeles County Department of Medical Examiner-Coroner">Los Angeles County Coroner</a>'s office later announced that Coolio died from an accidental overdose of <a href="/wiki/Fentanyl" title="Fentanyl">fentanyl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heroin" title="Heroin">heroin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Methamphetamine" title="Methamphetamine">methamphetamine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Coolio was <a href="/wiki/Cremated" class="mw-redirect" title="Cremated">cremated</a> in a private <a href="/wiki/Ceremony" title="Ceremony">ceremony</a> with no <a href="/wiki/Funeral" title="Funeral">funeral</a>. Some of his ashes were then encased in jewelry, including necklaces, for his family to wear; the rest of his ashes went into an <a href="/wiki/Urn" title="Urn">urn</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<tbody><tr>
<th>Year

<th>Title
</th>
<th>Role

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox" style="font-size:88%; vertical-align:middle;"><caption class="infobox-title" style="font-size:110%;">Coolio awards and nominations</caption><tbody><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data" style="text-align:center;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox-subbox infobox-3cols-child collapsible collapsed"><tbody><tr><th colspan="4" class="infobox-above" style="background-color:#d9e8ff; <div style="background:#cec; width:100%; padding:1px;">Wins</div></td><td class="infobox-data infobox-data-b" style="width:60px; background:#FDD; text-align:center; vertical-align:middle;;padding:0;">
<div style="background:#ecc; width:100%; padding:1px;">Nominations</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#EEEEFF; padding:1px; font-weight: normal; text-align:center;"><a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="American Music Award">American Music Awards</a></th><td class="infobox-data infobox-data-a" style="width:60px; background:#9F9; text-align:center; vertical-align:middle;">

3</td><td class="infobox-data infobox-data-b" style="width:60px; background:#FDD; text-align:center; vertical-align:middle;">
6</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color:#d9e8ff;">Totals<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup></th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width:50%; font-weight:normal; text-align:center;;background:#9F9;">Wins</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align:center;;background:#9F9;">5</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="width:50%; font-weight:normal; text-align:center;;background:#FDD;">Nominations</th><td class="infobox-data" style="text-align:center;;background:#FDD;">14</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-below" style="background:#d9e8ff; text-align:center;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1127642053">.mw-parser-output .hidden-begin{box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;padding:5px;border:none;font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .hidden-title{font-weight:bold;line-height:1.6;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .hidden-content{text-align:left}</style><div class="hidden-begin mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="border:none;"><div class="hidden-title" style="text-align:center;">Note</div><div class="hidden-content mw-collapsible-content" style="">
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-101">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Certain award groups do not simply award one winner. They recognize several different recipients, have runners-up, and have third place. Since this is a specific recognition and is different from losing an award, runner-up mentions are considered wins in this award tally. For simplification and to avoid errors, each award in this list has been presumed to have had a prior nomination.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Coolio's 1995 song "Gangsta's Paradise", a remake of Stevie Wonder's "Pastime Paradise" received several awards, including <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Solo_Performance" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Solo Performance">Best Rap Solo Performance</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a><sup id="cite_ref-grammy_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Video" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Video">Best Rap Video</a> and <a href="/wiki/Best_Video_from_a_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Video from a Film">Best Video from a Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>. Coolio himself received several awards, including Favorite Rap/Hip Hop Artist at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> in 1996. At the Grammy Awards in 1997, Coolio received three nominations: <a href="/wiki/Best_Rap_Album" class="mw-redirect" title="Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> for <i>Gangsta's Paradise</i>, Best Rap Solo Performance for "1, 2, 3, 4 (Sumpin' New)", and <a href="/wiki/Best_R%26B_Vocal_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Best R&amp;B Vocal Performance by a Duo or Group">Best R&amp;B Vocal Performance by a Duo or Group</a> for "Stomp". Overall, Coolio received five awards from fourteen nominations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Music_Awards">American Music Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: American Music Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> is an annual awards ceremony created by <a href="/wiki/Dick_Clark" title="Dick Clark">Dick Clark</a> in 1973. Coolio received one award from two nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-rotn_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotn-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grammy_Awards">Grammy Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Grammy Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Awards</a> are awarded annually by the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Recording_Arts_and_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences">National Academy of Recording Arts and Sciences</a> of the United States. Coolio received one award from six nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-rotn_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotn-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1050814317">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="MTV_Video_Music_Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coolio&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: MTV Video Music Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a> is an annual awards ceremony established in 1984 by <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>. Coolio received three awards from six nominations.<sup id="cite_ref-rotn_102-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rotn-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1050814317">
